рд╕рд╛рдпрдгрдГ

рдЕрдерд╛рд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рджреНрд╡рд┐рддреАрдпреЗ рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгреЗ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдкрддрд┐рд░реВрдкрдЪрд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рдЧреНрдиреЗрдГ рдХрд╛рд▓рдордиреНрддреНрд░рд╛рддреНрдордХрддреНрд╡рдВ, рдЪрдпрдирдлрд▓рдВ рдЪ; рдореГрддреНрдпреБрд░реВрдкрддреНрд╡рдВ рдореГрддреНрдпреБрд░реВрдкреЛрдкрд╛рд╕рдирд╛рдлрд▓рдореБрдкрдзреЗрдпрд╛рдирд╛рдорд┐рд╖реНрдЯрдХрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд╕рдЩреНрдЦреНрдпрд╛, рддрджреНрд╡рд┐рднрд╛рдЧрд╢реНрдЪ, рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯрдХрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдЪ рд╕рдВрд╡рддреНрд╕рд░рддрджрд╡рдпрд╡рд╛рд╣реЛрд░рд╛рддреНрд░рдореБрд╣реВрд░реНрддреНрддрд╛рддреНрдордХрддреНрд╡рдВ рдордиреНрддреНрд░рд░реВрдкрддреНрд╡рдВ рдЪ рд╕реНрдкрд╖реНрдЯрдорд╛рдореНрдирд╛рдпрддреЗ ред рддрддреНрд░ рдкреНрд░рдердордВ рд╕рдВрд╡рддреНрд╕рд░рд░реВрдкрдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдкрддреЗрд░рдЧреНрдиреАрд╖реЛрдорд╛рддреНрдордХрддреНрд╡рдорд╛рд╣- рд╕рдВрд╡рддреНрд╕рд░реЛ рд╡реИ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдкрддрд┐рд░рдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ рд╕реЛрдореЛ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ рдЪрдиреНрджреНрд░рдорд╛ рдЗрддрд┐ ред рд╕рдВрд╡рддреНрд╕рд░рд╛рддреНрдордХрдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдкрддрд┐рд░реЗрд╡рд╛рдЧреНрдирд┐рд░рд┐рддреНрдпреБрдЪреНрдпрддреЗ ред рд╕реЛрдореЛ рд░рд╛рдЬреИрд╡ рдЪрдиреНрджреНрд░рдорд╛ рдЗрддреНрдпреБрдЪреНрдпрддреЗ ред рддрдЪреНрдЪрдиреНрджреНрд░рдорд╕реЛ рд╡рдЪрдирдореБрддреНрддрд░рддреНрд░ “рдпрдГ рд╕ рдЙрджрдХреНрд░рд╛рдорджреЗрд╖ рд╕ рдЪрдиреНрджреНрд░рдорд╛рдГ”- (рд╢. рдк. резреж ред рек ред реи ред реирен) рдЗрддрд┐ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдкрддреЗрд╢реНрдЪрдиреНрджреНрд░рддреНрд╡реЛрдХреНрддрд╛рд╡реБрдкрдпреБрдЬреНрдпрддреЗ ред рд╕рдГ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдкрддрд┐рдГ рд╕реНрд╡рдпрдореЗрд╡ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╕реНрддрдореНрдмрдкреБрддреНрд░рд╛рдп рдпрдЬреНрдЮрд╡рдЪрд╕реЗ рдпрдЬреНрдЮрдЛрд╖рдпреЗ рдЖрддреНрдорд╛рдирдВ рд╕реНрд╡рд╕реНрд╡рд░реВрдкрдВ рдкреНрд░реЛрдЪреЗ; рдХрд┐рдорд┐рддрд┐ ? рддрджрд╛рд╣- рдореЗ рдордо рдпрд╛рд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ рдЬреНрдпреЛрддреАрдВрд╖рд┐ рд╕рдиреНрддрд┐ рддрд╛рд╡рддреНрдпреЛ рдореЗ рдЗрд╖реНрдЯрдХрд╛рдГ рдХрд╛рд░реНрдпрд╛рдГ рдЗрддрд┐ рдкреНрд░реЛрд╡рд╛рдЪ рдЗрддрд┐ рд╕рдореНрдмрдиреНрдзрдГ рее рез рее

Eggeling
  1. Verily, Praj─Бpati, the year, is Agni, and King Soma, the moon. He himself, indeed, proclaimed (taught) his own self to Yaj├▒avacas R─Бjastamb─Бyana, saying, ‘As many lights as there are of mine, so many are my bricks.’

Eggeling
  1. Now in this Praj─Бpati, the year, there are seven hundred and twenty days and nights, his lights, (being) those bricks; three hundred and sixty

enclosing-stones 1, and three hundred and sixty bricks with (special) formulas. This Praj─Бpati, the year, has created all existing things, both what breathes and the breathless, both gods and men. Having created all existing things, he felt like one emptied out, and was afraid of death.

  1. And because he made himself twenty-four bodies, therefore the year consists of twenty-four half-months. With these twenty-four bodies of thirty bricks each he had not developed (sufficiently). He saw the fifteen parts of the day, the muh┼лrtas 9,

as forms for his body, as space-fillers (Lokampr╠ес╣З─Бs 10), as well as fifteen of the night; and inasmuch as they straightway (muhu) save (trai), they are (called) ‘muh┼лrt─Бс╕е’; and inasmuch as, whilst being small, they fill (p┼лr) these worlds (or spaces, ’loka’) they are (called) ’lokampr╠ес╣З─Бс╕е.’

That one (the sun) bakes everything here, by means of the days and nights, the half-moons, the months, the seasons, and the year; and this (Agni, the fire) bakes what is baked by that one: ‘A baker of the baked (he is),’ said Bh─Бradv─Бja of Agni; ‘for he bakes what has been baked by that (sun).’

  1. He then looked round over all existing things, and beheld all existing things in the threefold lore (the Veda), for therein is the body of all metres, of all stomas, of all vital airs, and of all the gods: this, indeed, exists, for it is immortal, and what is immortal exists; and this (contains also) that which is mortal.

Eggeling
  1. Praj─Бpati bethought himself, ‘Truly, all existing things are in the threefold lore: well, then, I will construct for myself a body so as to contain the whole threefold lore.’

  1. He then arranged the two other Vedas into twelve thousand Br╠еhat─лs,–eight (thousand) of the Yajus (formulas), and four of the S─Бman (hymns)–for of that extent is what was created by Praj─Бpati in these two Vedas. At the thirtieth arrangement these two came to an end in the Paс╣Еktis; and because it was at the thirtieth arrangement that they came to an end, there are thirty nights in the month; and because it was in the Paс╣Еktis, therefore Praj─Бpati is ‘p─Бс╣Еkta.’ There were one hundred-and-eight hundred 14 Paс╣Еktis.

рд╕рд╛рдпрдгрдГ

Eggeling
  1. Into these three worlds, (in the form of) the

fire-pan 18, he (Praj─Бpati) poured, as seed into the womb, his own self made up of the metres, stomas, vital airs, and deities. In the course of a half-moon the first body was made up, in a further (half-moon) the next (body), in a further one the next,–in a year he is made up whole and complete.

Eggeling
  1. Whenever he laid down an enclosing-stone 19, he laid down a night, and along with that fifteen muh┼лrtas, and along with the muh┼лrtas fifteen eighties (of syllables of the sacred texts) 20. And whenever he laid down a brick with a formula (yajushmat─л), he laid down a day 21, and along with that fifteen muh┼лrtas, and along with the muh┼лrtas fifteen eighties (of syllables). In this manner he put this threefold lore into his own self, and made it his own; and in this very (performance) he became the body of all existing things, (a body) composed of the metres, stomas, vital airs, and deities; and having become composed of all that, he ascended upwards; and he who thus ascended is that moon yonder.

рдЗрддрд┐ рд╢реНрд░реАрд╕рд╛рдпрдгрд╛рдЪрд╛рд░реНрдпрд╡рд┐рд░рдЪрд┐рддреЗ рдорд╛рдзрд╡реАрдпреЗ рд╡реЗрджрд╛рд░реНрдердкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢реЗ рдорд╛рдзреНрдпрдиреНрджрд┐рдиреАрдпрд╢рддрдкрдердмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрднрд╛рд╖реНрдпреЗ рджрд╢рдордХрд╛рдгреНрдбреЗ рдЪрддреБрд░реНрдереЗ рд╜рдзреНрдпрд╛рдпреЗ рджреНрд╡рд┐рддреАрдпрдВ рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрдореН рее (резреж-рек-реи) рее

Eggeling
  1. Now when he (the Sacrificer), being about to build an altar, undergoes the initiation-rite,–even as Praj─Бpati poured his own self, as seed, into the fire-pan as the womb,–so does he pour into the fire-pan, as seed into the womb, his own self composed of the metres, stomas, vital airs, and deities. In the course of a half-moon, his first body is made up, in a further (half-moon) the next (body), in a further one the next,–in a year he is made up whole and complete.

[рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдЦреНрдпрд╛рдирдВ рдПрдХреЛрдирддреНрд░рд┐рдВрд╢рддреНрддрдореЗ]

Eggeling
  1. And whenever he lays down an enclosing-stone, he lays down a night, and along with that fifteen muh┼лrtas, and along with the muh┼лrtas fifteen eighties (of syllables). And whenever he lays down a Yajushmat─л (brick), he lays down a day, and along with that fifteen muh┼лrtas, and along with the muh┼лrtas fifteen eighties (of syllables of the sacred texts). In this manner he puts this threefold lore into his own self, and makes it his own; and in this very (performance) he becomes the body of all existing things, (a body) composed of the metres, stomas, vital airs, and deities; and having become composed of all that, he ascends upwards.

Eggeling
  1. And he who shines yonder is his foundation, for over him he is built up, on him he is built up: from out of his own self he thus fashions him, from out of his own self he generates him. And when

he who knows this departs from this world, then he passes into that body composed of the metres, stomas, vital airs, and deities; and verily having become composed of all that, he who, knowing this performs this sacrificial work, or he who even knows it, ascends upwards.
